<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="background:#efefef; border-top:1px solid; border-top:1px solid #aaa;text-align:center;"><div class="sidebar-list-title-c"><a href="/wiki/Policy" title="Policy">Policy</a></div></div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content"><div class="hlist hlist-separated">

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="background:#efefef;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_sidebar" title="Template:Politics sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_sidebar" title="Template talk:Politics sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez,_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1723" data-file-width="1545" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg/220px-Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg/330px-Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg/440px-Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez%2C_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Richard_L%C3%B6wenhez,_Salbung_zum_K%C3%B6nig.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard I of England</a> being <a href="/wiki/Anointing#Royalty" title="Anointing">anointed</a> during his coronation in <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, from a 13th-century chronicle.</div></div></div>
<p>A <b>monarchy</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Government#Forms" title="Government">form of government</a> in which a person, the <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> for life or until <a href="/wiki/Abdication" title="Abdication">abdication</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(political)#monarchy" title="Legitimacy (political)">political legitimacy</a> and authority of the monarch may vary from restricted and largely symbolic (<a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>), to fully <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a> (<a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>), and can expand across the domains of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_succession" title="Order of succession">succession</a> of monarchs in many cases has been <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditical</a>, often building <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynastic periods</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">elective</a> and <a href="/wiki/Self-proclaimed_monarchy" title="Self-proclaimed monarchy">self-proclaimed</a> monarchies have also happened. <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy_(class)" title="Aristocracy (class)">Aristocrats</a>, though not inherent to monarchies, often serve as the pool of persons to draw the monarch from and fill the constituting institutions (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Diet_(assembly)" title="Diet (assembly)">diet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_court" title="Royal court">court</a>), giving many monarchies <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchic</a> elements.
</p><p>Monarchs can carry various titles such as <a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">emperor</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_regnant" title="Empress regnant">empress</a>, <a href="/wiki/King" title="King">king</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_regnant" title="Queen regnant">queen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raja" title="Raja">raja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">tsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">sultan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">shah</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Pharaoh" title="Pharaoh">pharaoh</a>. Monarchies can form <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal unions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Realm" title="Realm">realms</a> with <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> through personal association with the monarch, which is a common reason for monarchs carrying several titles.
</p><p>Monarchies were the most common form of government until the 20th century, by which time <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a> had <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_monarchy" title="Abolition of monarchy">replaced many monarchies</a>. Today <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_current_sovereign_monarchs" title="List of current sovereign monarchs">forty-three sovereign nations</a> in the world have a monarch, including fifteen <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a> that share <a href="/wiki/Charles_III" title="Charles III">King Charles III</a> as their head of state. Other than that, there is a range of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_current_constituent_monarchs" title="List of current constituent monarchs">sub-national monarchical entities</a>. Most of the modern monarchies tend to be constitutional monarchies, retaining under a constitution unique legal and ceremonial roles for the monarch, exercising limited or no political power, similar to heads of state in a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>.
</p>
