<td>
<table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Republican</a> forms of government:
</td></tr>
<tr style="font-size:90%">
<td>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#3355dd; color:white;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">Presidential republics</a> with an executive presidency separate from the legislature</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#f0e847; color:black;"> </span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">Semi-presidential system</a> with both an executive presidency and a separate head of government that leads the rest of the executive, who is appointed by the president and accountable to the legislature</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9a33; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">Parliamentary republics</a> with a ceremonial and non-executive president, where a separate head of government leads the executive and is dependent on the confidence of the legislature</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#66bb66; color:black;"> </span> Republics in which a combined head of state and government is elected by, or nominated by, the legislature and may or may not be subject to parliamentary confidence</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<hr/>
<table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Monarchical</a> forms of government:
</td></tr>
<tr style="font-size:90%">
<td>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#e75353; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">Constitutional monarchies</a> with a ceremonial and non-executive monarch, where a separate head of government leads the executive</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ee1af9; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">Semi-constitutional monarchies</a> with a ceremonial monarch, but where royalty still hold significant executive or legislative power</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#801a80; color:white;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">Absolute monarchies</a> where the monarch leads the executive</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<hr/>
<table>
<tbody><tr style="font-size:90%">
<td>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#aa6f33; color:black;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">One-party states</a> (in principle republics)</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#6b8e23; color:black;"> </span> Countries where constitutional provisions for government have been suspended</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#808080; color:black;"> </span> Countries which do not fit any of the above systems (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Provisional_government" title="Provisional government">provisional government</a> or unclear political situations)</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Currently, there are 43 nations and a population of roughly half a billion people in the world with a monarch as head of state. They fall roughly into the following categories:
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_realms">Commonwealth realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Commonwealth realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_III" title="Charles III">King Charles III</a> is, separately, monarch of fifteen <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a> (<a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Commonwealth of Australia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Commonwealth of the Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Independent State of Papua New Guinea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Federation of Saint Christopher and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a>). They evolved out of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> into fully independent states within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> that retain the King as head of state. All fifteen realms are constitutional monarchies and full democracies where the King has limited powers or a largely ceremonial role. The King is head of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Established_church" title="Established church">established church</a> of England), while the other 14 realms do not have a <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_European_constitutional_monarchies">Other European constitutional monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other European constitutional monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Andorra" title="Principality of Andorra">Principality of Andorra</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Belgium" title="Kingdom of Belgium">Kingdom of Belgium</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Luxembourg" title="Grand Duchy of Luxembourg">Grand Duchy of Luxembourg</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Liechtenstein" title="Principality of Liechtenstein">Principality of Liechtenstein</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway" title="Kingdom of Norway">Kingdom of Norway</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain" title="Kingdom of Spain">Kingdom of Spain</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sweden" title="Kingdom of Sweden">Kingdom of Sweden</a> are fully democratic states in which the monarch has a limited or largely ceremonial role. In some cases, there is a Christian religion established as the official church in each of these countries. This is the Lutheran form of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> in Norway, Sweden, and Denmark, while Andorra is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> country. Spain, Belgium, and the Netherlands have no official state religion. Luxembourg, which is predominantly Roman Catholic, has five so-called <i>officially recognized cults of national importance</i> (Roman Catholicism, Protestantism, Greek Orthodoxy, Judaism, and Islam), a status which gives those religions some privileges like the payment of a state salary to their priests.
</p><p>Andorra is unique among all existing monarchies, as it is a <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">diarchy</a>, with the co-princes being shared by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">president of France</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" title="Bishop of Urgell">bishop of Urgell</a>. This situation, based on historical precedence, has created a peculiar situation among monarchies, as:
</p>
<ul><li>neither of the co-princes is of Andorran descent;</li>
<li>one is elected by citizens of a foreign country (France), but not by Andorrans as they cannot vote in the French presidential elections; and</li>
<li>the other, the bishop of Urgell, is appointed by a foreign head of state, the pope.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_semi_constitutional_monarchies">European semi constitutional monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: European semi constitutional monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-constitutional_monarchy" title="Semi-constitutional monarchy">semi-constitutional monarchy</a> is a monarchy where the monarch rules according to a democratic constitution but still retains substantial powers. The <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Principality of Liechtenstein</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Principality of Monaco</a> are European semi constitutional monarchies. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_constitutional_referendum,_2003" title="Liechtenstein constitutional referendum, 2003">2003 Constitution referendum</a> gave the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_of_Liechtenstein" title="Prince of Liechtenstein">Prince of Liechtenstein</a> the power to veto any law that the <a href="/wiki/Landtag" title="Landtag">Landtag</a> (parliament) proposes, while the Landtag can veto any law that the Prince tries to pass. The prince can appoint or dismiss any elective member or government employee. However, he is not an absolute monarch, as the people can call for a referendum to end the monarch's reign. When Hereditary Prince Alois threatened to veto a referendum to legalize abortion in 2011, it came as a surprise because the prince had not vetoed any law for over 30 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[note 5]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_of_Monaco" title="Prince of Monaco">prince of Monaco</a> has simpler powers; he cannot appoint or dismiss any elective member or government employee to or from his or her post, but he can elect the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_of_Monaco" title="Minister of State of Monaco">minister of state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Monaco" title="Politics of Monaco">government council</a> and judges. Both <a href="/wiki/Albert_II,_Prince_of_Monaco" title="Albert II, Prince of Monaco">Albert II, Prince of Monaco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hans-Adam_II,_Prince_of_Liechtenstein" title="Hans-Adam II, Prince of Liechtenstein">Hans-Adam II, Prince of Liechtenstein</a>, are theoretically very powerful within their small states, but they have very limited power compared to the Islamic monarchs (see below). They also own huge tracts of land and are shareholders in many companies.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monarchies_in_the_Muslim_world">Monarchies in the Muslim world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Monarchies in the Muslim world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The monarchies of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bahrain" title="Kingdom of Bahrain">Kingdom of Bahrain</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Brunei_Darussalam" title="State of Brunei Darussalam">State of Brunei Darussalam</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hashemite_Kingdom_of_Jordan" title="Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan">Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Kuwait" title="State of Kuwait">State of Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Morocco" title="Kingdom of Morocco">Kingdom of Morocco</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Oman" title="Sultanate of Oman">Sultanate of Oman</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Qatar" title="State of Qatar">State of Qatar</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Kingdom of Saudi Arabia">Kingdom of Saudi Arabia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> generally retain far more powers than their European or Commonwealth counterparts. Brunei Darussalam, Oman, and Saudi Arabia remain absolute monarchies; Bahrain, Kuwait, and United Arab Emirates are classified as mixed, meaning there are representative bodies of some kind, but the monarch retains most of his powers. Jordan, Malaysia, and Morocco are constitutional monarchies, but their monarchs still retain more substantial powers than European equivalents.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_and_Southeast_Asian_constitutional_monarchies">East and Southeast Asian constitutional monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: East and Southeast Asian constitutional monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The kingdoms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bhutan" title="Kingdom of Bhutan">Bhutan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cambodia" title="Kingdom of Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Thailand" title="Kingdom of Thailand">Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> are constitutional monarchies where the monarch has a limited or merely ceremonial role. Bhutan made the change in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[27]</a></sup> Cambodia had its own monarchy after independence from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Colonial_Empire" title="French Colonial Empire">French Colonial Empire</a>, but it was deposed after the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> came into power. The monarchy was subsequently restored in the peace agreement of 1993. Thailand transitioned into a constitutional monarchy over the course of the 20th Century. Japan has had a monarchy, an <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">emperor</a>, according to legend, since Emperor Jimmu (reigned 660-585 BCE), making it the world's oldest existing monarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[28]</a></sup> After their defeat in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War_2" title="World War 2">Second World War</a>, Japan made great strides in limiting the power of the Emperor, giving most of it to the democratically elected <a href="/wiki/National_Diet" title="National Diet">National Diet</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_monarchies">Other monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Five monarchies do not fit into any of the above groups by virtue of geography or class of monarchy: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tonga" title="Kingdom of Tonga">Kingdom of Tonga</a> in <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Eswatini" title="Kingdom of Eswatini">Kingdom of Eswatini</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Lesotho" title="Kingdom of Lesotho">Kingdom of Lesotho</a> in Africa; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatican_City_State" title="Vatican City State">Vatican City State</a> in Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Sovereign Military Order of Malta</a>. Of these, Lesotho and Tonga are constitutional monarchies, while Eswatini and the Vatican City are absolute monarchies.
</p><p>Eswatini is unique among these monarchies, often being considered a <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">diarchy</a>: the King, or <a href="/wiki/Ngwenyama" title="Ngwenyama">Ngwenyama</a>, rules alongside his mother, the <a href="/wiki/Ndlovukati" title="Ndlovukati">Ndlovukati</a>, as dual heads of state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This was originally intended to provide a check on political power. The Ngwenyama, however, is considered the administrative head of state, while the Ndlovukati is considered the spiritual and national head of state, a position which more or less has become symbolic in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> is the absolute monarch of the Vatican City State (a separate entity from the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>) by virtue of his position as head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and Bishop of Rome; he is an elected rather than a hereditary ruler, and does not have to be a citizen of the territory prior to his election by the cardinals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Malta" title="Order of Malta">Order of Malta</a> describes itself as a "sovereign subject" based on its unique history and unusual present circumstances, but its exact status in international law is a subject of debate.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>, the position of head of state is described in Part III of the 1960 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Samoa" title="Constitution of Samoa">Samoan constitution</a>. At the time the constitution was adopted, it was anticipated that future heads of state would be chosen from among the four Tama a 'Aiga "royal" paramount chiefs. However, this is not required by the constitution, and, for this reason, Samoa can be considered a republic rather than a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kim_dynasty_(North_Korea)" title="Kim dynasty (North Korea)">ruling Kim family</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-un" title="Kim Jong-un">Kim Jong-un</a>) has been described as a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-35">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-37">[32]</a></sup> or a "hereditary dictatorship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DPRKMonarch_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-DPRKMonarch-38">[33]</a></sup> In 2013, Clause 2 of Article 10 of the new edited Ten Fundamental Principles of the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="Workers' Party of Korea">Korean Workers' Party</a> states that the party and revolution must be carried "eternally" by the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baekdu" title="Baekdu">Baekdu</a> (Kim's) bloodline".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-39">[34]</a></sup> This though does not mean it is a <i>de jure</i> absolute monarchy, as the country's name is the Democratic <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Republic</a> of Korea. 
</p><p>The al-Assad ruling Syria (<a href="/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad" title="Hafez al-Assad">Hafez al-Assad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> ) have also been described as a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-35">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-36">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-37">[32]</a></sup> or a "hereditary dictatorship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DPRKMonarch_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-DPRKMonarch-38">[33]</a></sup> After the death of Hafez Al-Assad in 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Syria" title="Constitution of Syria">Constitution of Syria</a> was <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Constitution_of_1973#History" title="Syrian Constitution of 1973">amended for the minimum age of the President to change from 40 to 34</a>, which allowed 34 year old Bashar al-Assad to become president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-39">[34]</a></sup> This though does not mean it is a <i>de jure</i> absolute monarchy, as the country's name is the Syrian Arab <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Republic</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Long_form_titles_for_the_country">Long form titles for the country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Long form titles for the country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Kingdom: Bahrain, Belgium, Bhutan, Cambodia, Denmark, Eswatini, Lesotho, Morocco, Netherlands, Norway, Saudi Arabia, Spain, Sweden, Thailand, Tonga, United Kingdom</li>
<li>State: Kuwait, Qatar, <i>Japan (de facto)</i>, Vatican City</li>
<li>Principality: Andorra, Liechtenstein, Monaco</li>
<li>Federation: Saint Kitts and Nevis, <i>Malaysia (de facto)</i></li>
<li>Commonwealth: Australia, Bahamas</li>
<li>Sultanate: Oman</li>
<li>Nation: Brunei Darussalam</li>
<li>Grand Duchy: Luxembourg</li>
<li>Independent State: Papua New Guinea</li>
<li>Emirate: United Arab Emirates</li>
<li>None: Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Canada, Grenada, Jamaica, Japan, Malaysia, New Zealand, Saint Lucia, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines, Solomon Islands, Tuvalu</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Now substituted with the concept of <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocracy</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Malaysia is a special case. Malaysia’s head of state, the <a href="/wiki/Yang_di-Pertuan_Agong" title="Yang di-Pertuan Agong">Yang di-Pertuan Agong</a> (often translated as "King"), is elected to serve a five-year term. However, he is elected from among the federation's subnational monarchies, each of whom inherit their position and rule for life.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Examples are <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cromwell" title="Richard Cromwell">Richard Cromwell</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kim_il-Sung" title="Kim il-Sung">Kim il-Sung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Somoza_family" title="Somoza family">Somoza family</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duvalier" title="François Duvalier">François Duvalier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Duvalier" title="Jean-Claude Duvalier">Jean-Claude Duvalier</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad" title="Hafez al-Assad">Hafez al-Assad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">Kennedy family</a> in the United States and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nehru-Gandhi_family" title="Nehru-Gandhi family">Nehru-Gandhi family</a> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. See <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_families" title="List of political families">list of political families</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the end, this referendum failed to make it to a vote.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.dictionary.com/browse/republic" rel="nofollow">"The definition of republic"</a>. <i>Dictionary.com</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFWimmerFeinstein2010">Wimmer, Andreas; Feinstein, Yuval (October 8, 2010). "The Rise of the Nation-State across the World, 1816 to 2001". <i>American Sociological Review</i>. <b>75</b> (5): 764–790. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1177%2F0003122410382639" rel="nofollow">10.1177/0003122410382639</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:10075481" rel="nofollow">10075481</a>. <q>Sovereignty has a domestic and an external component. Domestically, a written constitution claims a nationally defined community of equal citizens as the political (and moral) foundation of the state and foresees some institutional representation of this community (not necessarily a freely elected parliament). Internal sovereignty thus stands in opposition to dynasticism, theocracy, feudal privilege, and mass slavery. [page 773]</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=American+Sociological+Review&amp;rft.atitle=The+Rise+of+the+Nation-State+across+the+World%2C+1816+to+2001.&amp;rft.volume=75&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.pages=764-790&amp;rft.date=2010-10-08&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1177%2F0003122410382639&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A10075481%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.aulast=Wimmer&amp;rft.aufirst=Andreas&amp;rft.au=Feinstein%2C+Yuval&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMonarchy"></span></span>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Monarchy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
